<span id="freeTextContainer4530903530728504912">Cool and glamorous, they appear to be a successful couple on a holiday. Yet Damian and Carrie Rose are psychopathic murderers for hire. On this picture-perfect vacation island, their target is Peter Macdonald, a dashing young American who forsakes a life of leisure to confront cold-blooded terror. But when they clash in a shocking endgame, a hideous truth will emerge - one</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4530903530728504912">Cool and glamorous, they appear to be a successful couple on a holiday. Yet Damian and Carrie Rose are psychopathic murderers for hire. On this picture-perfect vacation island, their target is Peter Macdonald, a dashing young American who forsakes a life of leisure to confront cold-blooded terror. But when they clash in a shocking endgame, a hideous truth will emerge - one that can destroy them all.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_161845585">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161845585" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1453804-brett-tompkins" class="left imgcol" title="Brett Tompkins"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1220307192p2/1453804.jpg" alt="Brett Tompkins" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/161845585?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 19, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1453804-brett-tompkins" class="user" title="Brett Tompkins">Brett Tompkins</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2505725.Season_of_the_Machete" title="Hardcover 9780613707084" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer161845585">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6811535155724543864">Simply dreadful. I read a bunch of reviews on this book and none of them were very good, so I can't say I wasn't warned. But like so many others, I am a completist, and I can't read all of Patterson's books without reading the bad ones as well. I don't know exactly why this book was so bad; it was just boring. There were times when I had read 20 pages and could not remember a single word, but I had planned out my entire evening. The character development was almost non-existent. About 150 pages</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6811535155724543864">Simply dreadful. I read a bunch of reviews on this book and none of them were very good, so I can't say I wasn't warned. But like so many others, I am a completist, and I can't read all of Patterson's books without reading the bad ones as well. I don't know exactly why this book was so bad; it was just boring. There were times when I had read 20 pages and could not remember a single word, but I had planned out my entire evening. The character development was almost non-existent. About 150 pages into the book I was asking myself, "who the hell is Peter?!" Turns out he was one of the main characters. <br /> This is the third of Patterson's first books that I have read, and two out of the three were terrible. The other one was re-released 10 years later so maybe it was revised to make it good? I'm beginning to wonder whether it was experience that made his novels better, or when he started letting other authors write for him? I'm sure glad I only paid a quarter for this book at the library book sale. On the good side, I've got this one out of the way and I can now say I've read it. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6811535155724543864">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer188832659">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15346455268508828453">It is hard to believe that a crime/thriller writter like Patterson turned out this book. A choppy writing style, back and forth snippits, and predictable plot twists made this a book that was almost painful to get through. The last third did pick up a bit, which helped (at least enough for me to plow through and finish). I did like the ending, but despite being left open for a potential sequel, it looks like Mr. Patterson (thankfully) has not opted to write. With the proper writer and director,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15346455268508828453">It is hard to believe that a crime/thriller writter like Patterson turned out this book. A choppy writing style, back and forth snippits, and predictable plot twists made this a book that was almost painful to get through. The last third did pick up a bit, which helped (at least enough for me to plow through and finish). I did like the ending, but despite being left open for a potential sequel, it looks like Mr. Patterson (thankfully) has not opted to write. With the proper writer and director, it may not be a bad movie however. But I'm sure Hollywood would just turn it into another lame slasher film.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_41325208">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41325208" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1196851-aaron" class="left imgcol" title="Aaron"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1213718341p2/1196851.jpg" alt="Aaron" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/41325208?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 30, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1196851-aaron" class="user" title="Aaron">Aaron</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer41325208">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1975405194001529429">The island of San Dominica, a popular Caribbean tourist destination, is thrown into chaos when a series of brutal slaying on the beaches start to take place. Each victim is brutally murdered and slashed by machetes.<br /><br />A mafia family with the hopes of adding some excitement to the island have hired Damian and Carrie Rose to commit the murders. Each is designed to look like the work of local rebels hoping to overthrow to government. The use of the machetes is supposed to help that image.<br /><br />What has made</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1975405194001529429">The island of San Dominica, a popular Caribbean tourist destination, is thrown into chaos when a series of brutal slaying on the beaches start to take place. Each victim is brutally murdered and slashed by machetes.<br /><br />A mafia family with the hopes of adding some excitement to the island have hired Damian and Carrie Rose to commit the murders. Each is designed to look like the work of local rebels hoping to overthrow to government. The use of the machetes is supposed to help that image.<br /><br />What has made the crimes so difficult solve is the total lack of witnesses. This changes quickly with an American hotel worker whose girlfriend becomes a victim is able to identify some important identifying details that will help tie the crimes to Damian.<br /><br />As the story progresses the rate of the murders increase, even bringing some examples to the American mainland. This quick-tale is typical Patterson when it comes to writing style, but there is no strong narrator that helps tie the plot together. Instead, the reader is rushed from one murder to the next from the perspective of each victim, with the events tied together with a mysterious series of journal entries about the times. As a result, it is hard to really build a connection with anyone.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1975405194001529429">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/1899570-mike" class="left imgcol" title="Mike"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Mike" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1381732859?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1899570-mike" class="user" title="Mike">Mike</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1381732859">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15731231555393909661">Well, it's called Season of the Machete...it ain't about butterflies and puppy dogs. This is an older Patterson work, and while he was still finding his feet, I liked that it was a different feel than the ones he's been churning out the last 10 years. The storytelling trick (this is all after the fact somewhat and told through the lens of the villian selling a diary of the events) lent a non-obtrusive time keeping slant to the fast paced story. The characters are mostly one-trick ponies but when</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15731231555393909661">Well, it's called Season of the Machete...it ain't about butterflies and puppy dogs. This is an older Patterson work, and while he was still finding his feet, I liked that it was a different feel than the ones he's been churning out the last 10 years. The storytelling trick (this is all after the fact somewhat and told through the lens of the villian selling a diary of the events) lent a non-obtrusive time keeping slant to the fast paced story. The characters are mostly one-trick ponies but when every other page involves a massacre of some sort, that's ok. It's an ok quick beach-type-read (although considering everytime someone goes on the beach in the book they are taking their life into their hands, may not take that literally) and definitely one to take a look at if not familiar with Patterson before his book a month pace of late.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one!</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer477353787">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17136704474322647833">I wonder what the purpose of this book was? I couldn't be to entertain. It surely wasn't to shock or titillate. James Patterson, whom some love and some hate, makes me wonder how he ever got famous after writing something this pointless in his early career. It was oddly unfocused and, when decipherable, transparent. Overall, it was deplorable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_196740965">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196740965" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5860033-lynn" class="left imgcol" title="Lynn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1378088338p2/5860033.jpg" alt="Lynn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/196740965?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5860033-lynn" class="user" title="Lynn">Lynn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer196740965">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9587527251619512519">I'll start by saying that Season of the Machete wasn't as bad as I was led to believe by some of the reviews I'd read. There was a story in there, somewhere - it was just hard to figure out exactly what it was and who the good and bad guys were. This book meandered all over the place and there were just too many characters and too many towns to keep track of. In Patterson's defense, though, this was only his second book (dating back to the late 70's).<br /><br />Season of the Machete starts off in Las Vegas</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9587527251619512519">I'll start by saying that Season of the Machete wasn't as bad as I was led to believe by some of the reviews I'd read. There was a story in there, somewhere - it was just hard to figure out exactly what it was and who the good and bad guys were. This book meandered all over the place and there were just too many characters and too many towns to keep track of. In Patterson's defense, though, this was only his second book (dating back to the late 70's).<br /><br />Season of the Machete starts off in Las Vegas with a meeting of a number of underworld types. Pay close attention to that chapter, because you may need to refer to it again to keep it all straight. By midway through the book, I had forgotten what the plan was, and why.<br /><br />I was also convinced until more than halfway through the book that it was written by someone other than James Patterson, and he just slapped his name on it. It really didn't "sound" like him at all. I thought perhaps this was an early experiment with co-authors (or in this case, ghost writers), but then decided I was wrong when he introduced a peripheral character named John Sampson. John Sampson is the name of Alex Cross's best friend, and having that same name crop up here cannot have been a coincidence.<br /><br />I wouldn't urge people to go out and buy this book, but if you're like me and have to read everything ever written by the authors you love, you will be able to make it through this one.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9587527251619512519">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer234314086">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5565228076234613924">This is my first James Patterson book, I can't say I was impressed with it however. It was not horribly bad, I did give it a 4 star rating after all and that is only because of the last hundred pages or so. Towards the end of the book the excitement picked up a whole lot and that's the only reason it has a 4 star rating. All the way through the book I was thinking that this is going to be a 3 star book but I like I said the ending changed that. I have heard great things about Patterson, I've hea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5565228076234613924">This is my first James Patterson book, I can't say I was impressed with it however. It was not horribly bad, I did give it a 4 star rating after all and that is only because of the last hundred pages or so. Towards the end of the book the excitement picked up a whole lot and that's the only reason it has a 4 star rating. All the way through the book I was thinking that this is going to be a 3 star book but I like I said the ending changed that. I have heard great things about Patterson, I've heard that he's a great writer; but I'm not really sold on that idea of him being that great. Granted yes this is only his second novel he wrote, but it wasn't so bad that I wouldn't give him another shot if I ever got a hold of another one of his books. My grandmother is a huge fan of him so I would like to like him but I'm just not sure. I may get a hold of another one of his book one day and try him out again but that would be only if someone gave me the book to read I wouldn't go out and buy one.<br /><br /><br />The writing style in this book wasn't to my liking all that much. It could have used a little bit more detail and it jumped around a lot. I like to be able to picture what I'm reading and I was not able to do that very well with this book. It was a grainy photo for me. And on top of that I found two or three grammar errors in the book and that just throw me off a little bit.<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_38675883">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38675883" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/946028-jbradford" class="left imgcol" title="JBradford"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1329373507p2/946028.jpg" alt="JBradford" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38675883?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 25, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/946028-jbradford" class="user" title="JBradford">JBradford</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38675883">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6081509275927232536">Patterson wrote this book back in 1977, making it one of his earliest works; he got better. It is typical Patterson, except that its hero is almost too low-keyed to be a hero. The novel reads much like a journalistic account of the plot developed by the baddies, Damian and Carrie Rose, who are lovers and also psychopathic murderers for hire. Their employers in this case are a strange combination of Mafia bosses and CIA-type federal agents, who agree to finance their plot to create a revolt on a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6081509275927232536">Patterson wrote this book back in 1977, making it one of his earliest works; he got better. It is typical Patterson, except that its hero is almost too low-keyed to be a hero. The novel reads much like a journalistic account of the plot developed by the baddies, Damian and Carrie Rose, who are lovers and also psychopathic murderers for hire. Their employers in this case are a strange combination of Mafia bosses and CIA-type federal agents, who agree to finance their plot to create a revolt on a picture-perfect tropical island for the sole purpose of creating an environment more hospitable to gambling casinos (it is not made clear why the CIA would want this, but the Mafia hope to own and run the gambling). The plot involves creating turmoil by killing a lot of people with machetes, and everything is going swimmingly until our non-hero, Peter Macdonald, a young American who works as a bartender in a hotel on the island gets involved. As is usual with Patterson, the end is not the end. The climax becomes twisted into a different climax, which then in turn gets twisted again. I’ll grant that there is a lot of suspense and excitement, but the book rubbed me a bit wrong, as I dislike to see bad things happen to good people, and there is a lot of that in this book. I had a real problem accepting some of the characterizations; I just could not believe that these people would do these things, and the Roses’ plot seemed a bit far-fetched to my way of thinking.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6081509275927232536">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <a href="/user/show/674412-kevin" class="user" title="Kevin">Kevin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer24850129">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7463037173704452658">When you want to instill terror in the hearts and minds of both the citizenry and tourists of the small Caribbean island of San Dominica, you use Damian and Carrie Rose. With the help of two other mercenaries, these two contract killers methodically stalk their targets and then slaughter them with a combination sniper/machete attack. What's worse is that no one has any idea what the Rose's look like, even the people that hired them, because they never leave witnesses. That is until Peter Macdona</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7463037173704452658">When you want to instill terror in the hearts and minds of both the citizenry and tourists of the small Caribbean island of San Dominica, you use Damian and Carrie Rose. With the help of two other mercenaries, these two contract killers methodically stalk their targets and then slaughter them with a combination sniper/machete attack. What's worse is that no one has any idea what the Rose's look like, even the people that hired them, because they never leave witnesses. That is until Peter Macdonald, in one of his island bike rides, inadvertently sees Damian and his two hired hands at work. The problem is that everyone in a position of authority believes the murders to be the work of an island revolutionary named Dassie Dred. Now, Peter is running for his life and trying to convince anyone who will listen, that he knows who is behind the killings. Very suspenseful and horrific writing by Patterson in one of his earliest novels. Although he uses pop culture references that tend to date the book, it still reads as though it would be valid in this day and age. This dating makes me worry about recent Patterson novels and how well, if at all, they will hold up 10 years down the road.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5860350949850848192">This was the second book ever written by James Patterson and as i had said in my last review for his first novel "The Thomas Berryman Number" I am not a particular fan of his earlier work, but also went on to say that his work does get better, this i know! "Season Of The Machete" follows that pattern exactly, a little bit better however not great. Although overall understanding the plot i had times where i was confused as to which way this novel was going? We have two hired assassins, The Roses,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5860350949850848192">This was the second book ever written by James Patterson and as i had said in my last review for his first novel "The Thomas Berryman Number" I am not a particular fan of his earlier work, but also went on to say that his work does get better, this i know! "Season Of The Machete" follows that pattern exactly, a little bit better however not great. Although overall understanding the plot i had times where i was confused as to which way this novel was going? We have two hired assassins, The Roses, Carrie And Damian, a husband and wife team who get hired on by the local criminal element to supposedly to liven up things on the Carribean island of San Dominica by commiting a huge variety of murders using a machete. Why anyone, even the mafia, would think this was a good idea to liven things up is beyond me?<br /><br /> Can't discuss the plot anymore then that as it's either too confusing or I don't want to deliver any spoilers, the court is still out on that one. Overall wasn't a fan of this book at all. I' am a completist so i finished this book however as i had said in his first book's review, had i only read both book 1 and 2 of his i probably would not have read anything else of his. Patterson still remains my favorite author presently and i dont hold those two books against himas we all had our beginnings.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer499538832">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11943708749311904620">A Wave Of Terror Sweeps An Island Nation.<br />-----------<br />John McDonald and his girl friend are on vacation to get away from it all. His girl friend is there for the sun and the sand. John is is there to try and forget about the experiences he had before he got out of the military. All is going well until one day John decides to go for a run on the beach. <br /><br />There had been reports that a revolutionary named Dredd had been committing horrible attacks on tourists in the area in order to make all foreigners</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11943708749311904620">A Wave Of Terror Sweeps An Island Nation.<br />-----------<br />John McDonald and his girl friend are on vacation to get away from it all. His girl friend is there for the sun and the sand. John is is there to try and forget about the experiences he had before he got out of the military. All is going well until one day John decides to go for a run on the beach. <br /><br />There had been reports that a revolutionary named Dredd had been committing horrible attacks on tourists in the area in order to make all foreigners leave the island for good. So when John hears gun shots, his army training kicks in and he drops to the ground. As the attackers finish off their victims, John and the shooter lock gazes. Instead of a island revolutionary the man appears to be a blond haired American. The man quickly disappears and John tries to alert the Island authorities. <br /><br />Little does he know that he has just gotten in the way of a vast conspiracy to control the island. Even worse he broke the number one rule that those behind the attacks have: never be seen, never let anyone know that the roses are causing the chaos. John McDonald must be eliminated.<br />----------------<br />This book was a little weird at first, but it gets good in the second half. The setup is a little slow and the “fish out of water” mentality that the main character seems to suffer from through the first part of the book is a little annoying, but once he figures out he has annoyed some dangerous people he turns his brain on.<br /><br />In some cases it's too little too late, but that seems to be a set up for the overall chase that is coming. Speaking of which the story does kind of follow a movie script kind of formula, but overall it does it well and does tie up most of the lose ends by the closing page. All in all a good read. I would recommend to those that like their thrillers to have a little suspense and a few twists and turns.m.a.c</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_154307219">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154307219" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2629627-dan-schwartz" class="left imgcol" title="Dan Schwartz"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442504143p2/2629627.jpg" alt="Dan Schwartz" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/154307219?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 14, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2629627-dan-schwartz" class="user" title="Dan Schwartz">Dan Schwartz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2629627-dan-schwartz?shelf=reviews" class="actionLinkLite">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154307219">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16386267163839974861">An interesting book. Not great, but not terrible either; a good middle ground. It was one of Patterson's earlier works and if you are familiar with his later works then you can tell. The story jumps around a great deal and some parts of the story are never fully explained. I do not want to give away any spoilers, so I will just say the main plot has some holes that Patterson did not even bother spackling over. On the otherside, the characters were pretty great and very interesting. I felt the ma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16386267163839974861">An interesting book. Not great, but not terrible either; a good middle ground. It was one of Patterson's earlier works and if you are familiar with his later works then you can tell. The story jumps around a great deal and some parts of the story are never fully explained. I do not want to give away any spoilers, so I will just say the main plot has some holes that Patterson did not even bother spackling over. On the otherside, the characters were pretty great and very interesting. I felt the main character was so-so and I found myself liking the villain much more (this was not the first time I found myself rooting for a villain in a Patterson novel, i.e. Swimsuit). Also, after reading this book it dawned on me that James Patterson is way to creative in developing plans to kill people and get away with it. I would never want to piss this man off so I chose (for my own safety) not to go below three stars on rating this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16386267163839974861">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12952284534281945175">I'll begin by saying I really enjoy reading books by James Patterson. This book was one of the few I didn't like so well. The writing was pure James Patterson. The story line, however, left me in a funk. As the title implies, machetes are involved in killings, grizzly, gruesome, disgusting, mutilating killings of random victims. Had this been the first book by Patterson that I read, I probably would not go on to read others. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9979661624486003375">Definitely a very different novel by James Patterson compared to his newer ones. But still a lot of action as a bunch of machete murders are occurring in San Dominica all masterminded by a couple Damian and Carrie. Only one person, Peter, has seen the elusive Damian. They are out to get him until they realize he could be useful in their get away as he IDs another man who looks like him. But do they ever really get away or does peter and the CIA figure out their game plan?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12935610046476646452">I don't usually read reviews until after I have read a book, and that was the case with this one. My opinion of the novel was justified, though, once I read other people's reviews. I kept waiting for something to happen in this one, something satisfying, something that would reveal the "why" behind the plot, but it never really came.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText12935610046476646452">I don't usually read reviews until after I have read a book, and that was the case with this one. My opinion of the novel was justified, though, once I read other people's reviews. I kept waiting for something to happen in this one, something satisfying, something that would reveal the "why" behind the plot, but it never really came. It was written in a way that made it a difficult read. I am not a big James Patterson fan, and this is the first novel of his I have actually read. It made me wonder why so many people enjoy his work.</span>

Patterson writes like the love child of&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText15778765309483087976\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;In clothing, Bermuda Shorts are a kind of casual formal wear - and in this collection of essays, Bermuda Shorts is the perfect metaphor for James J. Patterson\'s fundamentally serious but playful literary style. Patterson writes like the love child of Henry Miller and Mary Karr, with all the contradictions that implies -- a philosopher who thinks best over a glass of fine wine; an ex-Catholic still haunted by the image of the Crucifixion; an irreverent political satirist whose patriotism flies the flag of another iconoclast, Thomas Paine. Patterson grew up with a foot planted in each of two worlds -- one in Washington DC, the Capital of the Empire as he calls it, where the wheels of power spin, and one in rural Ontario, where his Canadian mother insisted the family spend their summers. His father, one of the wizards of twentieth century newspaper publishing, introduced him to the city\'s wheels of money and power, which he would later navigate as an entrepreneur, starting his first business at 20. But those Canadian summers introduced him to a different world - one where a cedar strip boat was better than any car, and where the ghosts of those who\'d previously inhabited the family\'s island house floated out over the water of Lovesick Lake. It is those two worlds that blend in this collection, in reflections both serious and playful, on what it means to be a man, an artist, an iconoclast, a patriot, a lover, as the 20th century rolls     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson">About James Patterson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson"><img alt="3780" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1284492096p2/3780.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7026976093691501659"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.com">Offical US Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk">Offical UK Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespattersonya.com">Offical James Patterson Young Adult Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.middleschoolbook.com">Offical Site for James Patterson's Middle School Series</a><br /><br /><br /><br />The subject of a <em>Time</em> magazine feature called, "The Man Who Can't Miss," James Patterson is the bestselling author of the past year, bar none, with more than 16 million books sold in North America alone. In 2007, one of every fifteen hardcover fiction books sold was a Patter</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7026976093691501659"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.com">Offical US Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk">Offical UK Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespattersonya.com">Offical James Patterson Young Adult Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.middleschoolbook.com">Offical Site for James Patterson's Middle School Series</a><br /><br /><br /><br />The subject of a <em>Time</em> magazine feature called, "The Man Who Can't Miss," James Patterson is the bestselling author of the past year, bar none, with more than 16 million books sold in North America alone. In 2007, one of every fifteen hardcover fiction books sold was a Patterson title. In the past three years, James has sold more books than any other author (according to Bookscan), and in total, James's books have sold an estimated 220 million copies worldwide. He is the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on <em>The New York Times</em> adult and children's lists and is the only author to have five new hardcover novels debut at #1 on the list in one year—a record-breaking feat he's accomplished every year since 2005. To date, James Patterson has had nineteen consecutive #1 <em>New York Times</em> bestselling novels, and holds the <em>New York Times</em> record for most Hardcover Fiction bestselling titles by a single author (63 total), which is also a Guinness World Record.<br /><br /><br /><br />From his James Patterson Pageturner Awards (which rewarded groups and individuals for creative and effective ways to spread the joy of reading) to his website <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.readkiddoread.com">ReadKiddoRead.com</a> (which helps adults find books that kids are sure to love) to his regular donations of thousands of books to troops overseas, Patterson is a lifelong champion of books and reading. His first foray into books for all ages was the critically acclaimed Maximum Ride series, which debuted on the New York Times bestsellers list at #1 and remained there for twelve straight weeks. The series has so far made appearances on <em>The New York Times</em> bestsellers lists ninety-four cumulative times, proving that kids of all ages love page turners. He captured the attention of boy readers with the Daniel X series, and his third series for readers of all ages debuted in December 2009 with <em>Witch &amp; Wizard</em>, which spent five consecutive weeks atop the <em>New York Times</em> bestsellers list.<br /><br /><br /><br />Patterson is the creator of the #1 new detective series of the past dozen years, featuring Alex Cross and including the Hollywood-adapted "Along Came a Spider" and "Kiss the Girls," starring Academy Award-winning actor Morgan Freeman. He is also the creator of the #1 new detective series of the past five years, featuring Lindsay Boxer and the other members of the Women's Murder Club, from which the ABC television drama series was adapted. He has authored books behind six films on the Hollywood fast-track, including the upcoming Maximum Ride movie forthcoming from Avi Arad, the producer of X-Men and Spiderman.<br /><br /><br /><br />He is the author of novels—from The Thomas Berryman Number (1976) to Honeymoon (2005)—that have won awards including the Edgar, the BCA Mystery Guild's Thriller of the Year, the International Thriller of the Year award, and the Reader's Digest Reader's Choice Award. And, he has won a Children's Choice Book Council's Children's Choice Awards "Author of the Year" award (2010).<br /><br /><br /><br />One of Forbes magazine's Celebrity 100, James made a guest appearance on the popular FOX TV show "The Simpsons" in March, 2007.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7026976093691501659">...more</a>

    </div>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/list/3780.James_Patterson">Books by James Patterson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
    <div data-current-user-id="false" data-use-wtr-tooltip="true" class="js-dataTooltip">
        <div data-placement="bottom-left" data-resource-id="13145" data-resource-type="Book" class="js-tooltipTrigger tooltipTrigger">
          <a href="/book/show/13145.Along_Came_a_Spider"><img width="50" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/books/1388272560m/13145.jpg" id="more_book_13145" /></a>
        </div>
        <div data-placement="bottom-left" data-resource-id="13148" data-resource-type="Book" class="js-tooltipTrigger tooltipTrigger">
          <a href="/book/show/13148.Kiss_the_Girls"><img width="50" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/books/1390010470m/13148.jpg" id="more_book_13148" /></a>
        </div>
        <div data-placement="bottom-left" data-resource-id="13137" data-resource-type="Book" class="js-tooltipTrigger tooltipTrigger">
